Many investors utilize risk/reward ratios to assess the expected returns of an investment relative to the level of risk they must assume to achieve those returns. A lower risk/return ratio is typically more favorable, as it indicates less risk for an equivalent potential gain.  Let's consider an example: an investment with a risk-reward ratio of 1:7 implies that an investor is willing to risk $1 for the opportunity to earn $7. In contrast, a risk/reward ratio of 1:3 suggests that an investor should expect to invest $1 in order to potentially earn $3 on their investment.
